The treasury of health conteynyng many profitable medycines gathered out of
Hypocrates, Galen and Auycen, by one Petrus Hyspanus translated into English by
Humfre Lloyd^ who hath added thereunto the causes and signs of every disease,
with the Aphorisms of Hypocrates, and Iacobus de Partybus redacted to a
certain order according to the members of mans body, and a compendiouse tabl^
conteynyng the purging and confortatyue medycynes, with the exposicyo of
certain names weyghtes in this book contained with an epystle of Diocles unto
king Antigonus.

Ecclesiast.xxxvii. The Lord hath created Physycke of the earth, and he that
is wise will not abhor it.

To the Gentil hearted Reader Humfrey Lloyde.
Although diverse learned me of no less judgment then practyse, have
berebefore translated and set forth sundry books, containing the most wholesome
and profitable precepts of Physic, wherein they seem to have openid and at
large declared al such things as seemed necessary and expedient to be had and
know in this our vlgare English tongue: yet never thelesse, I calling to
memory the notable s^ntence of Cicero, that every man is not alonly borne for
him self bu^ chifely to profit his native Country then his parents,
afterward his children and friends, seeking a means whereby I might profit
this my natyue Country, thought it best to traslate this little treatise which
was gathered out of the works of the most noble and Ancient phisicions
Hipocrates, Galene, Dioscorides, and Auicen by one Petrus Hispanus which
(although he chanced in a barbarous and rude time) was a man of great
knowledge and lunge practyse unto which work conteyninge alonly ye simple and
bare practyse, I did add before every chapiter as brefely as I could, the
causes and signs of the sicknesses and dyseases, trusting thereby both to
gratify and somewhat ease the pains of the reader so that he n^de not ^lles
where to seek the causes and signs of such diseases whose remedies were
coteyned in this book, and upon that consideration I did also translate and
add herunto the Aphorysmes of Hipocrates redacted unto such an order yt as the
members of manes body be disposed to receive some one disease and some another,
so the Aphorisms, which entreat of every disease that may happen to that
membre be gathered together into one chapiter beginning at the head and so in
order to the far: and also because men often times desire to know the names
and properties of compound medicines, I did translate a little book of such
compounds drawn out of mesue by one Iacobus de partibus, which work I have
redacted to the self same order that the aphorisms be in and furthermore
because I wold gratify the reader, and wold not he should be ignorant in the
names and weyghtes herin contained. I have hereunto added two tables, of the
which the first doth brefly express such symples compounds as do either
comfort or purge any disease or hurtful humour infectynge any member of mans
body, and the second expounds certain general names of medecines and
weyghtes commonly mentioned in this book and thereupon have made an end of this
rude simple work, employng my ^ole labour dylygence to set the same furthe as
truly as ny the authors mind as I could, not thinking but that there do some
faults remain therein both because the barbarous and arabic terms which the
author doth chyefly use, and of the diverse and sundry opynions of most notable
and well learned Phisicions as well in the names as in ye natures of herbs and
simples, and especially that we be either ignorant or destytute of English names
for a great sort of them, yet I did as nigh as I could follow Dioscorides and
in such things as I could not find in him I did confer Fuchsius, Ruellius and
Dorstemius together, and followed the judgment wherein they did al or the most
part of them agree, and in the Englyshing thereof I al other which intend any
such work are much beholden to Master Wyllyam Turner, who with no small
d^ligence hath in both his herballes most truly and syncerly s^t furth the
names and natures of diverse h^rbes, unto whose judgment and correccio and all
other learned in the most necessary science of Physycke, do I submyt this little
work and treatise, desiring them most heartily to take in good worth this my
first labour to accept my good will, not thinking it to be done to hurt any
man, knowing what a perylous thing it is for them that be not learned both in
the complectyons of men, Age, Regions, and time of the year, with the knowledge
of the Orygyne and causes of the diseases, to take upon them the cure of any
patient that rather they shall do hurt then good with the sole and only
practyse thereof except they do thereunto add great knowledge and perfyte
judgment had with painful study and long practyse, therefore I wold that all
such rash temerariouse persos should perfectly know, that it was never my mind
or will that this work should be set furth to maintain there fylthy lucre
and blind boldness, but ^hefely to be a toke and sign of the entye^ de^yre I
have to set furth the thing which should ^e acceptable and pleasant to the
Reader, ^lso I wold that it should be for ye use and pro^yte of such honest
persons as will modest^y and discretelye (either in time of necessyty ^hen no
learned Phisicion is at hand, or else ^onferryng with some learned man and vsynge
(...) council) minister the things herin coteyned go about the practise
thereof, upon these most honest godly cosyderacyos, I take upon me this heavy
burthe hard prouynce, therefore I shall most heartily desire the gentle reader to
pardon my audacity bear with my sclende^ judgment, and not to despise this
simple work because it is not garnished with colours ofrethorik and fine
polyshed terms, but rather to consider that Physike is an art content^ only
to be plainly and distinctlye taught and nothing desirous to be adorned and
decte with eloquence and gay painted sentences, wher^fore I trusting to the
syncer and indifferent^ judgment of the reader, do entirely desire him to pray
with me to him that created physick^ of the earth, and commanded that we
should honour the physycion, to preserve this Realm^ of England in most
prosperouse and continual health, and to endow the inhabitants thereof, with
perfyte understanding and the most desired knowledge of his holy word. Amen.

Places of scrypture which seem to make for the praise of Physyke.
MOses brought forth Israell frome the reddesee and they went to the
wilderness of sir, Exodi. 1^.
and they went three days in the wylldernesse and could find no water, and at
the last they came to mara but they could not drink of the waters for ye
byttern^s thereof, and Moses cried unto ye lord and he showed him a tree, and he
caste it into ye waters and they waxed sweet.

Also if you r^de over the.xiii.xiiii,xv, chapters of Leuiticu^ (where the
prestes be taught to dyscerne the Leprosy frome all other dyseases) you shall
find many things that make for the praise of Physycke.

H^zekish was sick to the death, and after he had prayed to the lord he sent
Isayahe unto him, Regist. 4. cap. 10.
who put a lump of figs upon the sore and he recoueryd.

Helyf^us the Prophet healed the nought and bitter waters of Ierycho and the
barennesse of the ground, Reg. 4 chap. 4.^
with casting salt into the spring thereof, he healed also Naaman of his
leprosy and the potage that was made of collyqu^ntyda.

The heart is glad of a sweet ointment and savour, Pro. 27. Tobi. 6.
but a stomach that can give good counsel rejoices a mans neighbor.

The angel said unto Tobias, take out the bowels of this fysh and as for the
heart, ye gall and the liver keep them by the for these things ^re necessary for
medicine.

For the falling of the Hear.
The Causes.
THe falling of the Hear is of two kinds, of the which the one is called
alopecya which is caused thrughe the malignite of vytiouse and noughty Humores
which rote and corrupt the rotes of the Hears whereby they fall away. The
other is called Deflunium capillo{rum} comes of ye rarytie of the skyne lack
of the Humore by the which ye hear be come furth and nourished for the
relaxatyon losnesse of the Skin is the cause why they be not steadfast and
want of their humour doth extenuat the same whereby they do fall away.

The Signs.
The signs or tokens be plain enough for in the first, the hear is more
lose in one place then in an other, and in the second they fall in all places
like.

Remedies.
Diosc. Isac.
IF thy hears fall, make lye of ye Ashes of Cvluer, dounge and wash thy head,
it is provide.

So do walnut leaves beaten with Bears sewet, restore ye hears that be
plucked away.

Seth the leaves of an Oak and the mydle rynd thereof in wa^er and wash thy
head, it is proved.

The ashes of little Frogs burnt Do cure the falling of the hear.

The ashes of Gootes dounge, mingled with oil, Galen,
doth engender hear.

The Decoctyone of a Mallowe Rote in water makes the scurffe of the head fall
of, if thy head be washed in that water, it is proved.

The water of the decoction of ye middle rynde of an elm thy head being o^ten
washed therein, Galen
doth the same.

Wormewoode stamped and laid to the temples doth quickly remedy the payne in
the head. Macer.


Stamp Parsley with the blood of an Hog, let them sethe in white wine and
afterward let it be strained through a cloth over cold water, and let the
Fat that flyteth or swimmith above be gath^red together and mengl^d with the
yolke of of a sodden egg and Mastike and Cumin and let the bare place be
anointed there with and there will hear grow quickly, it hath been provide.

Annoynte the place with raw Honey and sprynkle it over with the (...) over
with the Ashes of a grene Lacerte burnt, it engedreth much hear it is provide.

Diosc.
The blood of a Tortoise, if ye bare place be anointed there with engedreth much
hear and curethe the Leprye.

The same doth the Shell of the Snail being brent.

Gerard.
The Milk of an Ass doth make black the hear after a wounderfull manner.

Burn Barley bread with Salt, and mengle it with Bears sewet, anoint on what
place so ever thou wilt and the hears will grow there.

The Joyce of Sloes and Ink the utter rind or shale of a Nut braid and
tempered with vinegar so that they be moist, let them be applied for an
ointment and they do make the patients hear black.

The Ashes of a Goats claw, menglid and beaten with Pytche, remedies the
falling of the hear.

Let thy head be washed with Dogs peace, and thou shalt not be bald

Make lye of the ashes of the wod of Iuye, ye rind first pulled of wash an old
mas head therwyth and his hears shall be yelow two months space after.

These things following make hear to grow after Auicenius opinion first Oil
wherein a kind of flies called Cantharides be sod and boiled doth greatly dry
the fleme afterward let these be applied which follow. Oil of Eggs, Auicen.
bears sewet, Ashes of the herb called Condise or Lanary and of the pintle
and spleen of an Ass, the ashes of the ears and belly of an Hare burnt, ye
ashes of Laudatiu or Cist sage of sothernwod, of Teintworte and the ashes of
burned filberts also of wal^uttes, oil of Radyshe and Bayberys.

A Lacert and horse leches, minglyd together with the Oil called Laudanum and
let the place be anointed therwyth, and for a suerty the hear will grow, it is
provide.

Galen.
Burn the head, of a Fox together with the skyne unto ashes, and boyle a
Lacert (the head being cut o^) in oil mightilye a hole day, anoynte and
sprinkle that place with ye ashes where you will have hear grow. The same
thing workithe the ashes of Gotes doung, or of the claw of a Got.

Burn a quycke Snail upon a Tile and crushe it to ashes with.. of alume and
as much Mary of a Dere, sethe these in Wine a noint the baldnes. The same
thing doth the ashes of Bees myxte with oil.

Euphorbiu mingled with oil is wonderful good.

To take away Hear.
The Causes.
IT is a comin saying that if the one contrary be known the other is plain
and evident. Auicen.
So like wise he that knows why the hear fallethe or is little in quantytie,
is not ignorant why the Hear is much in quantytye and stedfaste, which
comes of the multitude of incorrupt humours and thycknesse of the Skine of the
head with streytnesse of the holes through the which the hear grows.

The Signs.
There is no declaracyon of the tokens necessary if a man do either se or
feel the head.

Remydes.
IF thou wilt yt the hear shulde never grow up again, pluck them up by the
rotes, anoint the place with the blood of a back or with the blood of a little
Frog, it is proved.

Put also to the place horse leches taken out of the standing water dressed
with strong Vinegar.

The ashes of a Colewortes stalk made in a plaster lets the growing up
of hears, it is provide.

The milk of a Bitch if the place be anointed therwt will not suffer ye hear
to grow. Galen.
The same affirmith Galene also, of ye blood of a bitch.

Let the joyce of a Gored, well delygently mengled with water be put on the
bare place.

Lapdanu the gum of an Ivy tree Emetes Eggs Arsenicke and Vinegar boude to
the place where ye will apply the and there will never hear grow.

Put the ashes of a grene frog brent in a bathe and al the hears y^ be
washed of ye bathe will fall away it is provide.

The Bran of Lupines or penny bean laid on the hearye place, Isac.
will make the hear to fall, and will not suffer other to grow.

The Joyce of Fumitorie myxte with gum of Arabyke and laid on the place the
hears first plucked out by the rotes will not parmytte the hears to grow.
Dioscor.


Been flower laid to the preuye mebres of a child, will not suffer the hear
to grow.

The things that let the growing up of hear after Auice be these opi^m,
Henbane, Auicen.

Against forgetfulness or drousynes.

The Causes.
THis disease is called in Greek of the effect Lethargus and in latin veternus
and is caused of cold and putrified phlegm which hath made cold, and filled
the brain.

The Signs.
The Lythargye comes with great sluggishness and such desire of sleep as cannot
be eschued, with great oblyuion, and forgetfulness so that they can scant tel what
they have done, nor make answer when they be spoken unto.

Remedies. Capi. iiii.
Against this disease of forgetfulness apply Few and red myntes with oil and
very strong Vinegar unto thy nostrils. Galen. Costan.


Burn thine own heate and mingle it with Vinegar and a little pytche and apply
it to thy nostrils, Constable.
for it wouderfully stirs quickneth yt persons diseased with forgetfulness. The
ligthes of an hog laid unto the head being shaven is very good

The blood of a Tortoys anointed on ye forehed is of much valour

The gal of a Crayne being made warm in a leaden vess^l doth thoroughly and
lightly stir up the deseased body if y^ nape of his neck be anointed
therwyth.

Fume made of Roes leather, doth myghtyly sterre him up.

Fume of Kyds skins doth quicken forgetful persons and those yt be infected
with the falling syknes and weme also that have their flowers stopte.

The sent or smell of Dog fennel, takes away sleep.

Grind Mustard sede with Vinegar, and rub it myghtyly on the plates of the
feet, and it doth quicken forgetful persons.

Sauery beaten and sodden in Vinegar laid in form of a plaster to the hinder
part of the head doth merrily awaken those yt are heavy with sleep.

Nothing doth better quicken forgetful persons then the smoke of a mans hear.

A drink made of Anacardiu is a peculiar remedy is this desease. Galen,


The smoke of Galbanum or of an h^rtes horne is best of al things

The skin of an Hare burnt and the ashes thereof droncke with calament heal
the lytargie.

For the Frensye.
The Causes.
THe Phrenisye comes of great abundance of blood or choler fyllyng up the
brains or paunicules thereof. Which choler if it be adust engenders a most
peryllouse peruiciouse phrenesy.

The Signs.
They which have the frenesye be troubled with a contynual fever and madness
with great watchings and little sleep, and when they wake they roar and cry
and cannot tell what they say or do, and if it come of blood they laugh, of
choler they fight and brawl and skat be ruled without Cords or Chains.

Remedies. Ca. v.
First let ye matter be put back with the joyce of Playntayne or morel and
Uyneger anointyng the teples therewith, then make a coif or cap of wax
terebintine and womans milk and put it upon the head, for it will ease the
pains provoke the pacyent to sleep.

Constable.
Let the fume of the matter be drawn downward with a suppository or clister,
with moderate rubbing of the hands and feet, then put a sponge dipped in the
decoction of Henbane or a whelp or a cock rypt over ye belly upon the head, or
ye lights of a swyne, also bind the arms and legs of the pacyent, and let
him smell Opium, camphory, Henbane, Basyl, Saffru or wax mingled with Rose
water, afterward anoynte the ears, eyes and nodle with mirth, storax,
Castoreum, or wash, the head, with Henbane or Smalage that have be sod in sweet
wine

Make an oyntmet of Dogfenel detain and oil of Roses, and anoint his head
therwyth and it shall cause him to sleep.

Also take of Opium. ii. of leven.ii. well beatyn with honey and vinegar and
anoynte the Pulses there with.

Make a plaster of Opium, henbane sede, and Sugar, mingled in the joyce of
lettys and lay it to his forehead.

Make a suppositori of Opium and oil of Uyolettes.

White Popie, and Henbane seed distempred with the white of an Egg and laid to
the forehead provokes sleep.

It is very good to let blood of ye vain which is in the myddel of the
forehead.

Take..i. of opium..ii. of black popy distempre them with populeon and the milk
of a woman that gives suck to a wench and lay it to the forehead.

The wax of the pacyentes ear, given him in drink causes him to sleep.

Seth Henbane in sweet wine and wash therewith thy ears temples nose thrilles,
it provokes sleep. The hot lights of a goat clapped to the head takes away
the frenesy so doth a Spoge dipped in warm wine and put to the left Pap,

It is very good to anoint ye forehead with oil of Roses, and to put a horsleche
to the forehead.

Constable.
Safron in all meates provokes sleep.

Lay to the pacyents head Saffro Mandrage and Opium he shall sleep.

Galen
If the head be anointed with oil of Roses, Dogfenell, and Castoru, it swageth
the pains and causes the pacyent to sleep. Galene.

Sprinckle the powder of Mandrage and Arsenike upon a shaven head, and the man
shall sleep.

If the face be washed with hot water of the Decoctyon of Popy ye pacyent

it hath ben provide.

For the head ache.
The Causes.
THis disease called in Greek cephalalgia and in arabike Soda comes sometimes
of great multitude of humours contained, in the head and sometimes of an
outward cause as of heate of the son of cold, of drunkenness, and of a
stripe, which be also diverse and sunday, but because the aucthore is so short
in his remedies (and I entende to write nothing here but that shall be
necessary for the understanding of him) I will pass the ou^r at this time.

The Signs.
Great pains in the head.

Remedies. Cap. vi.
THe joyce of ground yuie cast into the nostrils purges the head and
takes away the payne.

This doth purge the head wonderful well in every kind of head ache. take wax,
Masticke Pellitory, mustard seed, town crosses, Nigella romana, Stauisager,
Cynamon, of black and white, hellebore, of either.ii. ounces let these be well
puned and put in a bag of lynen clothe, then let ye pacyet fasting hold this
bag i his mouth chaw it betwixt his teeth, Gerard.
after wash his mouth with warm wine and Honey.

When al remedies fail a cantery in the hinder part the head helps

Against the Room.
The Causes.
A Great multitude of cold humours in the brain wych fall down to the nose and
throat.

The Signs.
This disease is soon known especially in cold weder.

Remedes. Capi. vii.
IF the Room come of a could cause lay hot Calamet or runnynge Time bruised
to the head.

Diosc.
An emplayster made of Garlic, cloves leaves stops ye humore causynge the
room.

Ysope bruiled in ye embres and so laid to ye head, stops ye Room. A
little bag full Darnel salt and anyse laid to the head is very good

A pomander made of the powder of Cub^bes, ma^ys, Laudanum, Gr^ke pitch doth
remove from the brain al superfluouse humours.

Maces and Cubebes chewed in the mouth do the same.

The joyce of colwortes cast in the ^ose thrilles doth purge the head. Mace^


Sorel punned with oil of Roses is good for the head ache.

Against the turn or daselyng^ in the head.
The Causes.
A Gross thycke humore in ye brain, fro the which rise vaporouse spirits and
move disordinatly about the brain and sumtimes these spirits or exhalatyons
come from the stomach.

The Signs.
The pacyent thinks that all things which he sees move and turn round,
and oftentimes falls down.

Annoynt thy forehead with opium, Mandrage hebane and Popy sede mingled with the
joyce of nightshade and oil of Uyolettes.

Rasis.
If it come of old pains in ye head dissolve Opium and Camphory in oil of
Wylow, and pour it into ye ears nosethryls, or put oil of v^olettes milk
into the nosethriles

on the fourth day let them be distellid keep it, as bawme it sharpneth the
sight, it clarifies the eyes it puts away the pynne and web.

Camphorye water betony have ben greatly proved to clear ye sight, stamp of
eyche together like quantity that myghtly well, and strayn the joyce out thereof
through a cloth and dis^ill or drop it into the eyes through a quyl.

spots of the ^ye.

Of the payne of the Ears.
The Causes.
Going or riding in cold wynd^s, or bathing in cold wat^r and sum times it
comes of a hot inflammation.

The Signs.
Great pains in the ears ether with hete or cold.

Remedies. Capi. xiii.
THe joyce of wild Cucumere leaves, Diosc.
takes away ye grefe of the ears.

Take and put the grene wood of an Asshe in the fyere, and save the liquor that
comes out at the end of the same put it into thine ears it causes the payne
of ye ears to cease and amends the hearing.

Stamp earth worms, the eggs of Emetes ye leaves of Rue together and being
sodden in oil strain them let faull one drop of that oil being warm into
thine ear it restores again the hearing, being ons lost.

Put oil scalion seed together, and megle thereto the joyce of lekes, and
wormewod, and womans milk sees them over the coals strain it, and put one
drop into thine ear and stop it fast with silk in the morning, after six
hours, take it out, turn the sore ear downward and wash it gently, it is a
goodly experymente.

Item in a hot cause, lettis made in a plaster is much worth. Hemp tow dipped
in the white of an egg is very good it is proved.

Item worms of the earth stapte with Rose water and applied to the ear are
very good also.

Item hot water with woman's milk only, applied for a plaster is of much
efficacy.

Rogerus.
Item if a little stone or a grain or any such like thing faull into a mans

strongely and a good while, and after set to his mouth again and suck.

ryndes of nuts or of the leaves of a peach tree.

somewhat opened on the lower part that fasteyneth to the tree in the morning
you shalt find there a worm al to pieces through the savour of the apple.

very much.

ears.

well.

The ^ynowes being very hot or cold or great quatity of humours, falling from

The payne is known well enough

For the Palsy.
The Causes.
Gross humours flowing to the synowes.

The Signs.
That the meb^r hath lost both s^nce and mocyon.

Remedies. Capi. xvii.
PArali^is is a sickness called the Palsy: wherein ether al the body or one
member or many mebres be mortified and be depryued of feeling and moving, it
happenith ether of an impostume stopping the rotes of the sinews, yt they
being depriued of y^ lively spirits which serve for them be come dead, or else
of the Fleumatyke humour gross^ and vndigested which stoppith the said places
some time of a stroke or foul, whereby the joints of the back bone are loused
and the synowes which come from the neck or nape of the head, are stopped other
while the synowes and the rotes of them hu^te with a bruyse engenders the
palsy, specially in a old man.

Lapida.
If the tongue be sodely wrythed through cold, make a whote gargarysme of the

Of the colyke and the payne called yliaca.
The Causes
The Colyeke comes of gross* and slimy humours or of wynd contained in the gut
colone, and yliaca is engedred of raw and corupt meates specially fat, and by
drinking cold drink after great heate.

The Signs
Grypynges and payne in the utter part of the belly with restriction thereof, and
belchynge and lothynge of meat do signify the Colycke, and yliaca is when the
pains and swelling is in the small guts with belchynge and murmuring in the
belly.

Remedies. Capi. xxviii.

grefe woderfullye.

takes the grefe away incontinent.

In Apostem, or gross humours therein contained.

The Signs.
The urine ever dropping at the yard with great desire to pysse.

To stop the flours
The Causes
The veins broken or opened, erosyons in the matrix or losinge of a child.

The Signs.
Change of colour, swelling in the feet and lack of appetite.

Remedies. Capi. xlvii.
IF the Flowers will not cease in there natural time, make a pessarie of goats
douge, and the joyce of shepherds purse or ribwort or Platayne, and put it into
the matrix.

Yarowe stampid with the water of the decoctyon of ypoquistidos, the flouers of
pomegranate, stops wonderfulli.

Make abath of these herbs Platayne, Shepherds purse, wild Tasill, and the
middel rind of an Oak, and afterward use this pessary. Take the powder of a
hearts horne, Ipoquistidos, Acacia, bole armeniake, new plaster, wax, Talowe
of a Got, and of ye which remaynethe make a plaster to the raynes share and
it stops Flowers on warrinsise. Likewise make a bathe of the rind of an
Oak, quicken beres or service, and plaster, this is of great efficacy.

As many grains as a woman doth drink of Coryander sede, so many days shall
the Flowers be stoppid.

Apessary or powder of ceruse or white lead minglid with powder of smallage,
doth meruelousli stop the Flowers.

The joyce of Lekes stops both the flowers and after burden,

Coral drunk stops the flowers, so doth the ashes of brent acornes cast
into the matrix dry and heal al fylthy and nociue hummours.

laid to the papes and kept a hole hour.

Rybwort drunk or made in a pessary stoppithe al flux of matrix and there is
no medicine comparable unto this.

The sede or rote of water lylly hath a peculiar virtue.

water of Pulyol drunk.

Cynabarys of some men callid dragons blood hath a maruelouse strength to stop

For the moder.
The Causes.
Much a bundance of humours with stopping of the flowers, or the cotencyon and
putrefaction of sede in the matrix, or great cold in the time of the flowers.

The Signs.
Sadness, pal^ colour sluggishness, weakn^sse in the legs, and in the
fytte, desyer to sleep, dotage, losing of all the senses and voice, with
cramps in the legg^s.

Remedies. Capi. xlviii.
IF a woman be greuid with the moder* stape netle leaves put the to ye matrix,
and let her also drink parsnepsede with wine for it is very good and losith
the suffocations and cleanses the sede contenid in the matrix.

A pessary of oil of bitter almondes, doth assuage the grefe utterly.

This is a principal medicine, let the woman smell to enphorbiu that she may
nese or blow it to her nostrils then shall she drink Castoreum cloves and
assofetida.

Also louage, Isope, wormewode Fern leaves, sod and made in a plaster and
laid from the nauyl to the share do wounderfullye help the moder.

Sethe wormewod and Fern or ether by it self and stamp them for a plaster
thereof doth break the pains of the moder.

A lynen cloth sod in the lye of the ashes of colewortes doth take awai the
ventositie of the matrix.

Triakle cloves and garlic dyssoluyd in strong hot wine, is present
medicine for the Moder, this have I provide.

Likewise doth a great ventose with much fire upon the share: also let her
receive stynkyng and filthy sauoures at her mouth a suffumigacion or diverse
sweet and odoriserous things beneth.

Rue sod and stamped in oil with hens grese and gose grese hot laid betwyxte
the nauyl and the share, is an excellent medicine.

Nettle sede drunk in wine doth a swag all pains in the matrix, take away
the ventositi thereof.

A suffumigacion of myrhe doth open the Matrix being inclosyd: so doth the
fume of Terebentine receiuid by the mouth.

Make a pessary of mint, calamint Sauery, hilwort and musk with castoreum put
this into the matrix, and let her smell assafetida, and rue this have I provide
to be wounderfull god.

Also Rue sod in water and put into the matrix asswagith the pains even so
doth the suffumygacyon of galbanum.

Rain water minglyd with strong vinegar and spout^d into the nostrils doth
soddenly drive down the moder, and like virtue have.xv grains of Peonye
drunk with wine.

For the Gout.
The Causes.
Much surfettinge and dronkenesse, to much accompaingin with women, imoderat
excercice, long stadynge, and such like,

The Signs.
Great pains and swelling in the joints chyeflye in spryngtyme and heruest.

THe iointe sickness is thus deuidid, into sciatica, which is in ye huckle bone.

salt Peter heleth the joint sickness and the gout.

is good for them yt have the palsy, and joint syckn^s.

distroyd, but their operacio is better and helth^uller.

Of the Agew called ephimera which endures but one day.
The Causes.
The vital spirits in a wonderful unnatural heate without putretactyon,
which comes of much watching, sadness, anger, hoger, or dronkenesse.

The Signs.
Great heate in the body with a fever ending in a sweat or vapour.

Remedies. Capi. lv.
First make a syrupe of the decoction of saunders, and the flowers of water
Lylyes, then let the pacyent avoid and eschew all things that burn the
heart* al that are gross and hot, and if ye vital spirits be in flamid
cheflye above all things bring the patient in a soft sleep, and let him
smell to Camfore with rose water, and violettes and such like, and minister
things that cause coldn^s and comfort the hart, as Margarites, sanders, and the
scrapynge of Ivory, or let him be anoyntid with oil of Rosis and Nenufar,
upon the breast and plasture thereon cold things teperid with Uenyger, and it is
very good against the heate: if ye natural spirits be inflamid, take cold
syrops and electuaryes that cause coldness, as are sugar, Rosys, and Uiolettes
and plaster the rosys sauders upon the liver, but if it be of a cold cause
beware of letting of blood, to engender more cold the^by specyally if it be
with a room.

Give unto the pacyent rose water newly made myxt with sugar or violettes, and
let him smell to basyl, yet let him not smell to other sweet sauoures, yt be
hot, and in a hot rewmatike cause, let him use a cold fomentatyon and
ointment, but chefelye if it come of over much labour, or copulation or heate
of ye air and such like, let the holownes of the hades and the souls of the
fete be anoyntid with oil of Uyolettes rosys woman's milk, also anoynte the
back bone, the forehead and teples with oil of rosys, Populion, woman's milk
that gives a woman child suck, and let his meat and drink be of light
dygestyon, and cold, but if it be of over much labour or of over much emptines
he must be nourished with resumptiues and confortatyues, if he cannot sweet,
this will heate him incontinet and minister occasion unto the patient to sweet.

Let the leaves of Sallowe tree Holyhoke, Uiolettes and rosis, and such like
boyle together in water, wherein put a great clothe, and l^t ye pacyent be
wrappyd in the same being warm and coueryd therwyth till he sweet, and
afterward let him wash his feet arms legs in the same decoctyon.

Item the joyce of Cucumers with oil of rosys anoyntid upon ye pulsys and upon
the heart, Dyosco.
asswagethe the heate of the Ague.

Platearius had a certain paciet destytute of strength, and put him in a
bathe of water, wherein sodden Eggs were resoluid and after the bathing he
departed strong.

Put a grene Gored in paste, and bake it in an oven, and afterwrynge out the
joyce and put it into a pot and sethe therein Hens flesh or of some other bird
(first well washte with wine and salt) and a few grains of whet and Barlye
Lycorice, gum, of Arabike, dragos Rosys, flowers of water Lylys, fleworte,
Almondes, of the gum of ye Almound tree, Basil* Reasons, myrabolans, Sebesten
sede, the sedes of a gourd, Melon and Cucumer being al clean dressed put the in
a pot well closyd with clay, and let them boyle till the third part be washid
afterward strain it and put sugar to the strayner and make a syrupe thereof
and give it unto the patient, it restores very well, temperately colythe and
helthfullye comfortithe fayntinge persons.

Of a contynual Agew.
The Causes.
Abundance of putrefyed humours contained within the veins.

The Signs.
Continual heate and pains unto the end of the Fever,

Remedies. Capi. lvi.
TO mytigate the over much heate in a continual Agew, Macer.
sethe Coleworte leaves with oil of Rosys, and plaster it upon the stomach.

The same thing may be done of Willow leaves, Morel and flewort

A certain curious practicionar showed me for a certainty, ye Pympernell
drunk with warm water, takes away the contynual Fever.

Put the sede of Flewort hole in water all a night, Auycen
then let it be strained and put thereto Sugar, give it unto the patient it
colethe, and intolerable heate of sharpe agewes.

Syrup of nenufur doth mightily heal sharpe Agewes. (...)


Galen.
Item if the Agewe be not very sharpe, let the pacyent drink cold wine myxt
with water it openythe the stoppynges within, bringithe furth corruptyon
through ye urine and confortith weak members.

Diosco* says that if the patient drink a great deal of cold water the
intolerable heate wylbe extynguyshed thereby.

In this cause apples that are called bitter swetes are very good.

Of the tertian Fever.
The Causes.
Much choleric humour putrefyeng in the sensible parts of the body.

The Signs.
To have a fit every other day and not to endure above.xii. hours.

Remedies. Capi. lvii.
IF it be the right Tertian give unto the pacyent to drink, ye joyce of
Dendelyon before coming of the fit.iii. or.iiii. times and the Agewe shall go
from him this am I sure of.

The matter being digestyd cause thy self to be let blood in the fourth or fyft
hours before the coming of the fit, and if it so be there go before any tokens
of digestio, he shall have the Agewe no more.

The matter being digestid make a plaster upon the pulses of ye arms of the
lesser nettel that grows in a very dry and warm place stamped with much
salt, for shortly after the Fever shall cease.

Myngle Radyshe rote being stamped, with Wheat bran, and make a plaster*
apply it between the nauyl and the share that the matter being first digestid
he shulde not perceue the payne and wringinges this remedy hath ben provide
against al kind of Tertian fevers.

The joyce of Ribwort give before the fit do com, takith away ye same.

Of the same operation are.iii. platayn rotes stamped and drunk with water
before the fit come. Diosco,

Garlyke bound to the outward members of a man, takes away ye quodyane and

Putrefyed phlegm driven by nature to all the sensible parts of the body.

The Signs.
To have a fit every day about xviii, hours lunge.

Of a Quartain Fever.
The Causes.
Melancholy putrefyed having recourse to diverse parts of man.

The Signs.
To have two good days and the thryd a sore fit.

Remedies. Capi. lix.

the bigness of a bean, give unto the pacyent before the fit do come on him.

For a Carbuncle and venomous bytyng.
The Causes
Gross and hot blood having recourse to any one place.

The Signs.
A sore painful ulcer or boil with a foul scabbe as it were brennyd with fire
with a great heat fever.

Remedies. Capi. lx.
THe brain of a hen or potage made thereof, eat or applied to the place of
the grief is of more better operation the any thing else.

A patients own spittle is very good against venomous bitinges,

A scorpion stamped and applied to the grievous place, is contrari to her own
stinging, and other of her kid and therefore it is a wounderfull remedy.

Lyra.
A fig leaf or the rind of a fig tree stamped and applied, is very apt good
against venomous stingiges

Gotes blood warmyd over the fyere drunk, is of myghtlye operation against al
drynkinge of poysones.

Gotes dounge temperid with honey and put unto the stinged place, heleth the
same.

Ox houfes sodden and eaten with mustard, withstand al poison, so yt nothing is
able to hurt.

Dioscor.
Agrymony drunk with wine, is wonderful good against the venemouse bytinge of
a serpent, a dog or a man, and a carbuncle.

Take hounds tongue grene or dried and lay it to the Carbuncle stinged or
venomous place, and it will ripe it.

Mollen stampte and plasteryd, is of great efficacye against the stinging of a
serpent, or when a meber is wounded put the joyce thereof into the wound, and it
will cause the venom to issewe out.

Cressys stampte and mynglid with bran healyth the carbuncle plasteryd thereon.

The ordure of a man is very good oft times before brekyng forth and after.
Auycen

operation unto it. Dioscorids also affyrmith that they do help against poisons
and stinginges of serpents.

Cheruill and coluer foot are very good against the carbuncle: Gilbert
in ye danger of death give unto the patient milk mingled with wine water

The rote of brom put into a vesel of wine, preserves the drinkars thereof
from all poison it hath ben provide.

Nature purging all corrupcion from the inward parts of ye body.

The signs be evident to the sight.

Against a hollow ulcer or fistula.
The Causes.
A corrupt and sharpe humour in any membre.

The Signs.
A deep hollow ulcer narow and harde with al.

Remedies. Capi. lxii.
Against ye disease called fistula mingle the milk of wertwort, with the fresh
grese of a hog let them boyle a little together and incorporate the afterward
put thereto powder of myrhe and anoynte ye tent with all and put into the hole.

Wine of the decoction of spurge put into the holownes of the ulcer, healethe,
and of the same operation working is ye joyce of coluerfote. Take of both
kinds of plantaine, of coluerfote, coryandre, marigold yarow, Primrose, daysy
that groeth in meadows, ye tender stalks of dock, and Betony make the al to
powder or to a joyce and give it to the patient dyseasyd with the fistule, at
morning nountide and night, it is sovereign and heals al kinds of fistules
and hollow ulcers if they be curable if not the patient shall vomyt it up
again.

Powder made of a bogs head healith the fistule, the cancre, and al
fylthynes in hollow ulcers.

If the Fistule have many holes be not straight yet, Costan.
if a medicine may pierce into the there is nothing better the to put into the
holownes of them gotes dounge with warm honey myxt withal, for it losyth all
sw^lling, draws out rottennes purgyth foul and defylid senowes healith up
the fistule asswagith the Cancre and grefe thereof.

If the Fistule be outward put therinto ye joyce of coluerfote it healyth, if
it be inward drink it, and it healith also.

Time stamped with salt plastrid upon the fistule helith the same.

Mans dounge burnt having myxt therwyth pepper beaten to powder, kills the
fistule cacre above al things.

Sethe the joyce of Mollen with honey, skume the same till the ioyc^ be
consumed, then put thereto of the rindes of Pomegranates and of ye stones of
myrabosanes, apply it to the cancre, it helps in continent.

Take the joyce of a cow turd (in a woman) and of an ox (in a man) wash the
fistula with the ioice and apply the residewe thereto plasteryd, it helps
quickly.

Dioscor.
Put leaven in strong lye so apply it to the fistule, and so it shall be

and dioscorides affyrmyth ye same of the lye Isaac of the leave.

This potion is wonderful very often prouid of me, for it kills the Fistule
in what place soever it be draws out the corrupt and broken bones.

Take the rotes and leaves of platan, strawbery leaves, the leaves or seade of
Hepe, the leaves or sede of mustard, ye tops of sharpe dock, red colewort

potyon come furth by the mouth of the Fistule, which must always be kept open
with a silver pipe put into it, and keep upon it always a red colewort leaf,
it is of a wouderful operacio.

To heal an old Leprye. Auycen
Take a serpent of a dry hyl, and cut of the head thereof quickly, and the
tail, let her blede stur about the blod till the bleding cease, and afterward
let the Serpent be modified from his inwards, and let it be sodden cause the
patient to eat thereof every day. i. and drink ye wine where in the serpent
hath ben sodden, till the leprouse person be swollen and puffed up and be gynne
through Anguish to be in a manner beside him self, then put the patient in a
stew or hot house, and let the hole body of the patient be anointyd with the
liquor wherein the adder or serpent was sodden, for the hole flesh and skin
is thereby renuid, and so shall the patient be perfytly healid. Take a black
serpent the head being cut of, bury her till she be full of worms then let her
be dried, and give thereof unto the leporouse. i. with a syrope of honey every
day.

Put corn in water of the decoction of serpents, and fed hens with the same
corn, and let them drink ye same water, and there feathers shall fall of, and
when they be vnfetherid let them be sod, and let the leprowse person eat them,
and drink the water where in they were sodden and let him wash his hands, face,
and berd therewith.

This same experiment is said to heal the pockes for a certayntye in one day,

Of Wartes.
The Causes.
Gross and cold melancholy or Phlegm.

The Signs.
Every man knows a wart.

Remedies. Capi. lxv.
TO take a way Wartes make this experiment put the feel of Hens in the hot
Embres till the scales or skin thereof be seperatid, and shronke from there
legs and the same skyne warm rub the wartes three or.iiii. times, or more,
and it will drive the a way.

away the wartes and scabs that be in any place.

Pursland rubbed upon the wartes, pulls them up by the rotes by his own
property.

water that comes therout anoint the wartes, bunchis, Figs about, or give it
the patient to drink it shall cause them al to foul out by the rotes.

and reserve the liquor that comes thereof, blende it with salt and apply it,

To pourge the choleric humour down ward. Capi. lxxv.
TO purge Choleric humours downward by the belly, and that in helthful men:
first let the matter be digestid, with Oxizaccharum, or else with sirupus
Acetosus, the matter being digestid, pourge it with this medicine. Take of ye
electuari desuccorosatu oximel, resoluid with the joyce of rosis ana. ii. of ye
joyce of scamoni. a half mingle the together if you will you may give ye paciet
thereof tempered with wine or you may make thereof pills.

If it so chance that the matter be contained from the navel downward or in
any other part of the body, then myngle with the fore rehersyd medicines. ii.
of the powder of mirabolanes citrines, of al this make pills, and let them be
given to ye patient.

Of Melancholy natural. Capi. lxxvi.
TO purge natural melacholie in helthful men, fallen in the nether parts of ye
body, first digest ye matter with squillitike oximel, or else with some syroupe
made therefore, ye matter being digestid purge it with this medicine.

Take of Hierologodion. ii. of hiera rufi. i. of theodoricon emp. i. of honey
Anacardine.. mengle them together and make pills, and give it in the euenning
let them be sharpenyd with. i. of spurge.

If the matter which ought to be purged, be in the middell parts of the body,
as in the stomach, or in the inward of man thereunto must be applied laxatiues,
as Cassia fistula..c. or as the medicine above mencionid.

But if it be inseueral parts of the body as in the gout in such a case must
strong medicines be ministrid as is rehearsal of before, they ought to be
doubled.

Of purging burnt collar. Capi. lxxvii.
TO purge burnt collar or salt phlegm, let the matter be preparid with
oxisaccharum in three parts thereof the fourth part of a syrupe, of diuretike
things or of syrupes made of the joyce of Fumitori, and purge it with this
medicine. Take Catar: Imperial, oximel laxative, of each. ii. of Hierologodian.
i. of spurge. i. mengle them together and make pills give them in the evening.

pomegranates. ii. sugar a poud a half and the same is good against the
quartaine after the.vii. fit, the joyce of Germandre being doubled these
medicines are ministrid to: helthful grutched not greatly vexed wi^h fits of
the Agewe.

To pourge phlegm in quotidian Fevers. Capi. lxxix.
TO purge natural phlegm in quotidias, take of electuariu ducis. i. temper it
with warm water give it unto the patient to drink in the morning.

A Certain experiment agayns^ the heuines of the head. Take of Agaricke. v.
