Take of cloves, macys, Nutmigges, Galingale, Dragons blood anyse, comin ana.
i. as much of spurge as of the al and make a powder.

The aphorisms of Hippocrates redacted unto a certain order, according unto
y^ members of a mans body, and the dyseases that may fall in any of them.
Of the disposityon of the head. Capi. prim.
VRyne troubled like unto the water of an Ox or horse signifies pains in the
head.

Milk is evil for them that have the head ache,

If y^ pains be in ye nodle of ye head it is good to cut ye vain in ye forhed

If any matter or water flow out at his nose or ears which hath the head
ache, it takes away ye pains.

Whatsoever helthful man is sodely pained in the head therewith losyth his voice
routeth withal, he dies within seven days, if an Agew take him not.

Of the lethargye or forgetfulness. Capi. ii.
To tremble in a lythargy is very evil.

Of the payne in the head called subeth. Ca. iii.
IN this disease painful sleep is mortal.

Of to much watchynge. Cap. iiii.
Immoderat sleep or watching is very evil.

Of the Palsy. Capi. v.
PAlseys do commenly chance fro xl. years of age till.lx

It is hard to help a small palsy, but to heal a greuouse palsy it is
ympossible.

It is no matter what kind of spume or froth be about their mouths which be
strangled or have thhe palsy, and be not yet dead.

Of the madness called melancholia. Capi. vi.
A Swellynge or weakness endurynge a lunge time brings a mato a melancholy.

Peryllouse eruptons in al melancholyke dyseases, do signify either the palsy
a conuulsyon, blyndenesse or madn^sse.

The Hemorrhoydes be very good to such as be melancholyke.

Of Raging madness. Capi. vii.
IF he that is mad be take with a laxe or hidropsye, it is good

The Hemorrhoydes breaking out, take a way madness.

If a mad man use to laugh it is a laudable sign, but if he be very sad, it
is peryllouse.

If a mad man find ease in sleaping it is good, but if his rage increase, it
is to be fearyd.

Of the falling Evil. Capi. viii.
They which have the falling evil in their childhod be oft healed, but if they
be past.xxv. year old, they die for the most part.

The changing of place time, and age curethe the falling evil in young men.

Of the diseases in the synowes. Ca. ix
ALl cold things be noyouse to the synowes, the bones, ye teeth the brains the
mary in the back, unto those al hot things be profitable and good.

A sudden Fever heals y^ crape.

A convulsyon after sleep in an ague, is to be feared.

To be short breathyd in an ague is the sign of a convulsion.

A convulsyon or gripinges in the belly in sharpe agues, be very evil.

A convulsyon after the drinking of hellebore, is deadly.

To have a convulsyon with a sore wound is death.

A conuulsyon is perillouse to him that hath blede much.

A convulsyon or yeskynge after a great inadityon be very euell.

If a drunken man lose his speech have a couulsyo he shall shortly die.

A convulsion comes of immoderate fullness or emptiness so doth yeskynge.

Yeskinge, vomiting, a convulsio or m^dnesse coming upon him yt is payn^d in
the small guts are, to be fearyd.

The cramp or madness with much watching, is very perillouse.

He that is taken with a sore convulsyon if he live four days shall e^kape.

A convulsyon after a purgatyon is very perillouse.

If a yonge man being fleshy be taken with a distension of the synowes in the
Somer time. let him be washed with cold water for ye doth increase the heate,
and ye heate doth assuage his pains.

In sore wounds a convulsion or distencyon be very evil.

Of the drousynes in the head. Capi. ^.
TO dote or to be astonished after a blow or stripe is, very evil,

Of the members being set awry. Capi. xi.
IN a continual agew if the lyppes, the eyes, the brows or the nose stand
awry, so that the pacyent can not hear or see and be therewith very weke, he
shall dye shortly after.

Of the disposition of the eyes. Capi. xii.
OF the times of ye year if it chase the winter to be dry and ye northwind to
blow, the springtime moist with the southwynd, ye somer following there shall
many be troubled with blernesse, but of the contrary part if the winter be moist
with much southwind, the springtime dry with northwindes, men shall be likewise
vexed with dry blernisse.

If in autune, or Heruest there be much drought, and northwyndes, it shall do
good to moist persos and women, but other it shall vex with dry blernes.

When the times of the year be dry m^ny shall have bler eyes.

The southwynde blowing daily for a season, will engender daselinge in the
eyes.

Diseases of the eyes do cheflye rainge in somer.

In a continual agewe, if the eyes be wrythen a side, and the pacyent weak
and cannot see, it is a pr^sent token of death.

In all kinds of Fevers, and other diseases, voluntary tears be laudable*
but if they flow contrary to the pacyentes mind, they be to be fearyd.

It is very good* if he that is diseasyd in ye eyes be taken with a sode lax.

All dyseasys in the eyes be healyd either by drinking of sweet wynes, or with
baths of whote water or letting of blood or with a purgacio.

If a man be seek mark his eyes when he slepyth for if any white thing
appear betwixt the eye lids, and the patient have no great laxe nor
received any purgatio before, is a terrible and deadly sign.

Of the disposion of the ears. Capi. xiii.
Whosoever uses to void choler, and in ye mean while waxes defe, the laxe
stops, and of the contrary part, a sudden lax deiectyon of choler takes
away defnesse.

To wax defe in a continual agew (the pacyent being weak of body) is a
token of death.

Uoluntary bleding at the nose or a sudden lax doth take away the de^nes
which comes of an ague.

Of the disposition of the nose. Capi. xiiii.
THey whose nostrilles be full of superfluouse moystnesse, and have also their
nature or seade very waterish, be not helthful of body, and they that be
contrary enjoy continual health.

Horsnesse and continual fluxion of sneuil in old men, do in no meas wax
ripe.

A dry Somer with often northwynd and a moist Harvest with ye southwind, doth
engendre in ye next winter the head ache, ye cough horsenesse, and much
fluxyon of room by the nostrils, but if the Heruest be dry and the northwynd
blow, the room shall endure much longer. Old men be often grieved with
fluxyon of room and ye cough.

Much room contained in the stomach is changed within twenty days to plain
matter.

All cold things as snow and ise, do engender distillatyons.

Of the bledinge at the nose. Capi. xv.
OLd men and children do oft blede at the nose.

If it chance him that is seek of an agewe to blede, he shall have a laxe in
the decrease of his fever.

He that waxes deffe through an agewe bledithe at the nose shall recover his
hearing.

Who so is like to have an apostem in any of his joints and in the mean while
bleadeth at the nose is sure to recover his health.

If a woman whose flowers be stopped do chance to blead at the nose it is a
good sign.

Bleding at the nose or ears takes away the headake.

To have the cramp or to dote while the nose bledeth is an evil sign.

Of nesing. Capi xvi
IF a woman having the mother, or beig in pains of child birth, chance to
nese. it is very good.

Nesinge takes away belchinge.

All nesing that comes of the head is caused either of the brain being hot,
or the empti place of the head being very moist, for the air with in
contained brekith out through a narowe passage, and thereby causes the noise.

Of the disposions of the mouth tong. Capi. xvii.
YOnge children and infantes be often troubled with ulcers in the mouth, and to
much vomytinge.

Of al other men they which lisp, be most troubled with mani sieges, and
laxes.

Of the diseases in the teeth. Capi. xviii.
IT is the sign of continuance in an ague, to have much slimy matter about the
teeth.

When the teeth begin to grow children are pained with fevers, cramps, and
ytchinge of the gummes* espicially in the growing of the gum teethe.

Of the grefes in the throat. Ca. xix
OFtentimes diseases propre for the somer season do chance in autume, as the
squinancy, shortness of breath, and the pains in the flape that covers the
wind pipe.

A suffocatyon chancinge to him that hath an agew, and no swelling remain in
the throat, is a token of death.

If the squinancye fall down to the lights, and the patient live seven days,
the fluxion will turn to matter

If he that hath the squinancy do swell in the neckei, tis a good token for the
fluxion is driven outward.

He that hath an agew not being able to turn his neck, neither to swallow
his meat, without a manifest swelling in the throat, shall short lye dye.

Of the breast and lights. Cap. xx.
TO have the brethe somewhat stopped in an agew is an evil token, for a
convulsyon shall shortly follow, they which have swelling in their backs before
they be xiiii. year old coming of shortness of brethe, or a sore cough, shall
shortly dye.

If it chance a droken man suddenly to fall speechless, he shall shortly dye of
a conuulsyon, except either he fall to an agew, or else he receive his speech
again at the hour when the surfyt is digestyd.

They which suddenly are taken with pains in the head, therwyth lose their speech
route, they dye shortly, if they be not taken with an agew. Whosoever hath his
brains hurt any way, doth sodely lose his speech.

Of blood spyttynge. Capi. xxi.
YOnge men be chieflye troubled with spittyng of blood, consumptyons, hot
fevers, and the falling Evil.

The spyttel in a continual Fever being wane of colour, bloody, stinkyng, or
choleric, is an euel toke.

He that spits frothy blood is diseasyd in the lights.

If he that spits blood, spit therewith al filthy matter, it is an evil
sign.

To vomit blood without an agew is helthful, but in an ague peruicious

Of the pleurisye. Capi. xxii,
IF in the beginning of a Pleurysye the pacyent use to spit, it shortneth the
disease, but if it chance afward it prolongs the pains.

The Northwynd blowing a long season to gender, engenders colykes coughs, and
pleurisyes.

Pleurisyes, peripeunomyes, rewmes, and coughs do chiefli raygne in the
winter.

If he which hath the pleurisie, be not purged in.xiiii. days, the fluxyon
will change to matter.

The pleurisy once changed to matter, if the paciet be not purged with in
forty days after the brekinge furth of the matter, he shall fall to a
consumptyon.

A sudden laxe following a pleurysie or a peripeunomy, is very peryllouse.

They whose belchinge smellith ^umwhat sharpe or tart, be not given to the
pleurisye.

The frenesye in a peripeunomye is an evil token.

Whosoever having filthy matter in the void place of the stomach, or having
the hydropsy, is laced or brened, if all the matter or water issue furthe, it
is present death.

Of the consumpsion or ptisike. Cap. xxiii
AUtume or heruest is very yuill to the which be in a consumption.

A dry somer with much northewynd, and a moist heruest with southwyndes, do
engendre in the winter following coughs and rewmes, to diverse, consumptyons.

In consumptions purge downward, and upward.

They which be betwixt.xviii..xxv. be chieflye troubled with the ptisike.

If his spittell which has a consumpsition being cast upon coals do stincke,
and the hear fall of his head, it is a sign of death.

A sudden laxe to him that is in a consumptyon and his hear fall o^ is
deadly.

Milk is vnholsome to the which have the headake, or that be syke of any
fever, and to the which hau^ noise and wind in the hyer part of there belyes,
and that have choleric decoctions in hot fevers, or yt have lost much of
their blood, of the contrary part, it is good to such as have a consumption
without an agew, and also it may be ministered to them which have agewes long
time, if none of the abouesayd tokens do appear, to such as have been lunge
seek of a consumption.

Aptisike or laxe with spittynge of fylthy matter if the spittinge cease is
deadly.

Of the dispositions of the heart Ca. 24.
GReat brennynge in the stomach prickynge about the h^rt is an evil token in an
agew.

They which lose their strength of ^entymes without manifest occasio ^hall dye
suddenly.

Of the Paps. Capi. xxv.
IF the Paps of a woman whi^h is with child of two do wax little, ^he shall
lose one child, and if it be ye right Pap it is a man child, and if it be
the lift a woman.

If a woman, that neither is with child, another hath brought furthe a child,
have milk in her paps, she is past her Flowers.

Blood drawing to the paps of a woman, is a sign of the frenesy.

If thou wilt stop the flowers of a woman, put a great ventose upon her
paps.

Much milk yssuyng out of the tetes of a woman yt is with child, betokens
the child to be very weak and feeble, but if the paps be hard the child is
strong and helthful.

Like as the decreasing of the paps is a sign of the destructyon of the
child, so the hardness of the same signifies great pains, in the paps,
legs, knees, or eyes, and the life of the child.

Of the stomach. Cap. xxvi.
THe stomach is most hot in the winter and springtyme and then also the
slepes be longest.

Men can not well away with much meat in the somer and herueste, but meanly in the
spring, and best of all in the winter.

In all dyseases to be steadfast of mind, and to be content with such things as
be mynystred to him, is a laudable sign, but the contrary is very evil.

Drink of wine doth take away hunger.

If he which goes very dry to bed steppe, it is good.

If they which have certain murmuryng and wynd in their belyes, have great
pains in the loins, they shall have moist deiections, if ye wind do nether com
furth nor great multitude of vryne, and al these do chance in fevers.

If in a laxe or vomyt such things be purged as ought to be purged, it doth
ease the paciet and it is nothing greuouse, but if no it chances contrary.

Let such as can not easly vomit, be purged downward, but not in the somer.

In all kind of diseases if black choler be purged upward or downward
without a medicine, it is perillouse.

In the pains of the small guts called yl^aca, vomytynge, yeskynge,
convulsyon, or dotynge be evil.

A convulsion and yeskyng after a great purging, are to be fearyd.

A sudden and voluntary vomiting, heals him that hath had a lunge laxe.

Yeskynge is good to him which hath a heate swelling in the liver.

Of the diseasys in the liver. Capi. xxvii
AN agew takes away ye grefe and pains in the liver.

A wound in the brains, heart, midrife, small guts, stomach, or liver is
deadly.

If he whose liver mattreth be brenid and therout issue pure and whit matter,
he shall eskape, but if it be lik dregs he shall shortly dye.

Many diseases proper, to ye somer do chance in harvest, as quartaines and
Hydropsyes engendryd in the spleen.

If he which hath the dropsye be woundyd, it is harde to heal him. Whosoever
hath grypinges about the hauel, and pains in the loins and cannot be helped
bi purgatios or otherwise shall fall to a dry hidropsye.

The cough going before the hidropsye is evil, but in the hydropsy much
worse.

If they which he splenetike, have a blody flux which will long continue, they
fall to the hydropsye, or their meat shall cume through the vndygestyd and so
they dye.

A bloody flux, an hidropsy or madness after a frenesy, are laudable.

Whosoever have their liver full of water, and it break downward to the belly, it
is death.

If he that hath an agew be taken wi^h the yelow iandes ye.vii. the.ix. the.xi.
or.xiiii. day, it is laudable, if the right side wax not hard, but if it do,
it is contrary.

An agew takes away the pains under the syddes, if it be without great heate
and swelling.

Of the gaul and spleen. Capi. xxviii.
IF the yelow Iaundes, chance in an agew before the seventh day, it is evil.

They which have the yelow iandes be not full of wynd.

If there liver which have the yelowe ye iandes be hard, it is an evil sign.

A bloody flux is good to th^ y^ be splenetyke.

Of al kind of fluxyons. Cap. x^
IN a laxe diverse kinds of (...) be good, except they change to (...) as be
evil.

Black sieges like to fylthy b^ude bein^ voluntary be wounder^l evil wh^rther
they be with an (...) or without an agew, and ye de^ker to our they have, the worse
they be, but if these sieges com through a p^rgacion they be more laudable,
(...) although they be of diverse colours the be not evil.

To have a siege of plain m^cholye, or to perbreake the same in y^ beginning
of any disease is deadly

Whosoever is brought weak ether by some greuouse disease or siknes of lunge
contynuace, or by woudes received, or eny other way, and thereupon have a syege
of melancholy like to black blood he shall doutlesse they the day after.

A bloody flux beginning with a melancholic siege, is deadly.

Little peaces ^f flesh appearinge in a bloudye sie^e, be tokens of present
death.

Uayne desire to the stole in a woman with child, kills the child.

Tart or sharpe belching suddenly chancing to him whose meat comes through
him indigestid, is very good.

In log continuace of a bloudye flux, to abstain fro meat, is very evil if it
be with an ague much worse

A bloody flux is good to such as be splenetike.

A sudden bloody flux after a sincer or clean siege, is to be fearyd.

If a great laxe chance in a white morfewe, it takes away ye disease.

Frothy sieges in a flux, do declare the phlegm to come from the head.

It is an euell token in a sharpe agewe, to have a convulsion, or painful
gripinges in the belly.

Pains in the hyer parts of the belly, be more gentle of leasser peril then
they which be in the lower part.

If he which hath the strangurye, be take with the pains in the small guts
called iliaca, he shall dye with in seven days, except a fever take him with
much flux of vryn.

Of the fundament. Ca. xxx.
IF the Hemorrhoydes chance to such as be melancolike mad, or frentike, it is
laudable.

If he that hath lunge time had the hemorrhoydes be healyd, not one left open,
it is to be feared least he fall to a consumptyon or hidropsye

The hemorrhoydes be very good to such as have a melacholike madness, or great
grefe in the raynes.

Of the disposicyon of raynes. Capi. xxxi.
THey which have the pains in the raynes after.xl. years of age, can not be
healyd.

They whose vryne is full of gravel be seek of the stone, either in the raynes,
or in the bladder.

Dyseases in the raynes and bladder, are scant curable in old men. Little
bladders or bubles in a mas vryne, do betoken pains in the raynes, and lunge
diseasys.

The hyer part of the vryne fattye thick, is a sign of pains in the raynes
and sum greuouse disease.

If the above said tokens appear in such as be seek in the raynes, also have
sore pains in the muscles of ye back, if the pains be inward it signifies
an apostem in the inner parts, but if they be outward the apostem shall be there
also.

Much phlegm contained betwixt the stomach and the midrife, hauig no way to
the belly, is soon dissoluid if it issue by the veins to the bladder, and
thence furth in vryne.

Of the diseases in the bladder. Cap. 32.
IN moist and wet season, lunge agewes fluxes, rottenesse, ye falling evil,
the squinancy, and the palsye do cheflye raygne, but contrary in dry seasons,
cosumptions, blearnes goutes, straguryes bloody fluxes

Children be often grieved with pains in the throat, and falling of the jaws,
worms in the belly, stranguryes.

Old men have most comenlye these diseasys, shortness of brethe, room, the
cough, the straguri, difficulty of vryne, goutes, daselinge in the head,
pains in ye raynes, palses in their bodies out of just temperanse, y^ ytche,
watchings with moystnesse in the belly eyes and nosthriles dullness of sight, and
hearing.

If his water that is seek of an Ague be little in quantity thick and full of
crumes, th^rvpo his vryne follow much in quantity and thine it is very good,

Whosoever in an ague hath his water troubled like to the vryne of an ox or
cow, hath or shortly shall have the headake.

In such diseasys as shall be endyd the seventh day, there shall appear in the
pacyentes vryne a red cloud the fourth day with other reasonable tokens.

Uryne white and clear is not laudable, and especially in them which be
frentike or do^ing.

They which be like to have an apostem in their joints, be deliuerid thereof by
much vryne white thick as that which comes from such as have ben iiii. days
seek of an ague

Blood or matter in the urine doth declare ulcers, and biles, either in ye
raynes or blad^er.

Little pieces (...) flesh and hears in the vryne co^ ^rom the raynes.

Contents lyk^ bran in ye urine signify a Pocke or Scabbe in the bladder.

They which p^sse blood have a vain broken in th^ ^ynes.

If they which (...) blood or cromes, or else hau^ ^he ^tranguri, if the pains
be bene^h the beli about the share, the disease is in the bladder.

Gravel in the vryne betokens ye stone in the bladder.

He that pisseth blood or matter, he in whose urine skales do appear, or the
water have a strong smell, hath ulcers in the bladder.

Whosoever hath pustules or welkes in his yard, and if they break and the matter
run out, they shall be shortly hole.

To peace much in the night, doth betoken a lytlel siege.

The strangury chances to that parson which hath a hot swelling in the
fundament, or matrix, and to him whose reins do matter, yesking ever follows
the heate swelling in the liver.

Diseases in the raynes and blader, are hard to heal in old men.

Contetes in the botome of the urine like unto thick bran, signify the
disease lunge to continue.

If the water do appear unlike of substance, it betokens great mystemperace,
for diversity of humours within the body.

Drinking of wine, heals ye stragurye, and him yt cannot hold his water, it
is also good to let blood of the inner veins about ye ankle.

Of the membr^s of generatyon in men. Capi. xxxiii.
Likewise in men, either for the rarity of the body, the spirits goo out, so
that the seed ca not come to his due place: or for the thiknesse thereof the
humour cannot get furthe, neither wax hot for the coldness, and so it heaps
in yt place or else ye same thing comes of great heate.

A bone a gristel, a synow, and the the top of the yard being cut, will
nether grow nor join together.

Of the members of generation in women. Ca. xxxiiii
IF the winter be moist and warm the southwind blow, the sprig time dry with
northwyndes, those women that be then with child shall of every light occasyon
lose their children, the children then borne shall be weak and seckely, wherefore
they shall either dye strenght with, or else al their life time be, fayntye and
full of diseasys.

If a woman with child must ned^ be purged, let that be from ye fourth month
to the seventh, yet those suwhat leasse, but before four after seuin let the
receive no purgacions

The suffumigation of sweet odurs doth bring furth the flowers, is good for
diverse other things if it did not cause ye head to be drousi.

Lettynge of blood doth kill the child, but the nyer ye birth the more
perillouse it is.

If a woman with child be taken with any greuouse disease, it is death.

The fluxyon of the flowers takes a way vomiting of blood.

If the flowers stop it is good to blede at the nose.

It is perillouse for a woman with child to have a great laxe.

Nesynge is very good to her that hath the moder, or that trauaylethe of
childbirth.

She whose flours be evil colourid or that keep not their comyn cour^ had need
to take a purgatyon.

If thou would know whether ^ woman hath conceyuyd or no, geu^ her water and
honey mingled together to drink when she goes to sleep and if she feel
grypinges and pains in her belie she is with child, i^ she feel non she is
not.

A woman which hath conceuyd a male is well colouryd, but if it be a female,
it is contrary.

Those women which be very small and lean before they conceive, shall lose one
child before they wax gross, Those women which being mean of body, do lose
their children the second or third month without manifest occasyon, have the
closures of their wombs full of fylthy matter, wherefore they cannot sustain
the weight of ye child, but sodely break.

They which be very fat cannot conceive till they wax lean, for the ^outh of
their matrix is stopped ^p with fatness.

If thou will provoke the flowers ^ause the woman to nese, and in the ^eane
while stop her nose mouth

They which be with child have ^heyr wombs closed up.

If a woman with child be taken with an agew, and wax very hot, without
manifest occasion, she hath great pains in childebyrthe, or else ^he loses her
child with peril of her ^wne life.

If a convulsyon, and faintness ^ake a woman in ye time of her flou^s, it is
perillouse.

If the flowers have to much issue there do ensue diverse diseases, if they be
stopped there follows great grefe in the womb.

If a woman hath not conceived, thou wilt know whether she shall conceive or no*
let her be well coueryd with clothes, beneth let a suffumigacion be made of
hot things and odoriferous, for if the smell com up through her body to the
nose mouth, be sure yt she is not barayne of her self.

If a woman with child have her flours, it is impossible ye child should be
helthfull.

The flowers stopping with an ague or great cold, and the woman loathe her meat,
say she is with child.

The matrix cold and gross, or very moist, is not apt to conceive, for ye seed
is therein quenched destroyed. Likewise if it be dry and very hot, for the is
the seed lost for lack nourishment, but they whose matrix is of a mean
temperature be pletifull do often conceive, if you wilt know more rede above in
ye disposion of ye Paps.

Of the disposyon of the outward members Capi. xxxv.
IF two great grefes do happen in diverse mebres at one time, the gre^ter
takes away the leasse.

Pains in the knees and loins, or grypynges in the belly coming upon him that
hath non agew, do sygnifye that he shulde be purged down ward.

In painful fevers apostemes do often happen about the knees and chekes.

The sickness shall chiefly remain in that place which was grieved before it
began.

The joints of such as have had a fever for a long season, shall ache be full of
pustules.

Great pains swellynges in the joints with any brekinge or issue, do signify
that the gout or crape shall follow, and many be remedied with much washing with
cold water, for yt doth extenuat the humour and take a way the pains, for a
mean cold extinguishes.

Letting of blood doth utterly take a way such pains as begin at ye back,
thence remove to the arms. Enuches be never bald nor gouty.

Women have never the gout as lunge as they have their flowers.

A child hath never the gout until he hath known a woman.

All kind of goutes (if the inflammation be quenchid) within forty days, do
end.

All goutes do chieflye reygne in springtyme and harvest.

If the hipp bone fall out of his place after a long sciatica, there shall
much matter follow, or the leg will consume away, and the patient shall
halt, except he be brennyd.

Of the Fevers and Agues. Capi. xxxvi.
THe sickness it self, the time of ye year do plainly declare the time of the
fyttes, the chief time of the disease, the order in y^ fits.

Old men be never troubled with (...) sore agewes because their bodies be cold.

All sharpe diseasys are judged in fourtene days.

Quartanes in somer be very short in Autume much longer, in winter longest of
all.

It is much better that he which hath a convulsyon be take with an agew, then
he which hath an agewe be taken with a convulsyon.

If his flesh that hath a sore ague do either fall nothing away at al or
decay very much it is evil for the first betokenith long continuance of the
disease, and the other great wekenesse in the person.

At the beginning and ending of an agew, al things be of more stregthe then
in the chief part thereof.

In al diseases they be in leasse jeopardy to whose nature age, accusto, or
time of the year the sickness doth agree, then they with whom it doth in no
point agree.

Wh^n the somer is not unlike to the spring time you shall loke for much
sweting in al agewes.

In dry seasons there shall reygne diverse sore agewes.

All dyseases in the harvest season be perillouse and deadly, but in the
springtyme most gentle and easy.

In the somer these do chiefly reygne, contynual and brenynge agews tertyan and
quartayne fevers, vomyting, laxes, blernesse with ulcers in the mouth and
pryuy members. A cold stiffness chancig the sixth day in any fever doth take
away all judgment.

All fevers which do not intermite and give over the third day be perillouse,
but if the patient have no fyte that day there is no ieope^dy.

If great coldness take him which is very weke thrugh a continual agew it is
deadly.

If in a continual agew the outward members be very cold and the inward
parts hot and dry, it is a token of death

If in an agew pustules and pains chance in the joints, it is a sign that
the patient fedeth well.

In a continual Fever, if the lyppes, the eyes, the Nose or the mouth be
wrythen and out of fashion, so that the patient can not se nor here and
therewith all his body be weak, it is a sign that death is at hand.

A sudden laxe or dotage in a continual fever is deadly.

An apostem which doth not break at the first judging day in a Fever, doth
signify the lunge continuance of the disease.

Uoluntary tears in agewes be laudable, but they which flow against the
pacyentes will be to be fearyd.

Al Agewes with swelling in the foundament be evil except such as endure but
one day.

If he which hath an agew do sweat very much and the disease contynew it is
evil, for it betokens log syknesse and abundance of humours

He that hath a convulsyon or dissension in ye synowes, and thervpo an agew, is
suddenly delivered.

A tertyan not endid in seven fits shall continue lunge.

The yelowe iaundes coming upon him that hath a Fever before the seventh day is
perillouse.

To be afraid in his sleep, or to have the cramp is evil.

To be short brethyd in an agew is the sign of a convulsyon.

Soryful sighs in sharpe agewes be to be fearyd.

They which have the quartaine have seldom convulsyons, and if he which hath a
convulsion fall to a quartayne he shall be deliuerid from his conuulsyon.

If he which hath an agew sweat in these days following it is very good, the
third, the.v.vii, ix.xi.xiiii.xvii.xxi*xxvii, xxxi.xxxiiii. for ye swetes do
judge ye fever, but if they be otherwise, they declare lunge continuance of ye
disease great pains.

Of the diet to be observed in agues. Capi. xxxvii
IN al diseases of long cotinuance the pacyent most use little meat, exquisite,
but in sharpe diseasis yt is perillouse, yet to eat to little or to much be
both evil.

Secke m^n do more often err in vsynge little meat, then in that diet which
is somewhat larger, whereby they be oft hurt, yea and to such as be in health
small fare, and exquisite diet, is very perillouse, because they easly err
therein.

Unto extreme diseases extreme cures be necessary.

When the disease is most extreme and sharpe the pacyent shall by and by have
woderful pains, wherefore he most use most small and thin diet as the disease is
from extreme pains so most the diet amend.

When ye seknesse is most violet then most the paciet use least meat of al.

The phisicion most mark well wither the pacyent vsynge such small diet may
endure to the state strength of the disease, or wither the pains will first
assuage or no

If the sickness in the beginnynge be most fervent, then most the pacicyent use
little meat, but if the siknes be afterward most violent the pacyentes meat
most be somewhat before diminished, but in the beginning he most fed well that
he may be able to abide the disease.

The pacyent most forbear meat in the fyttes, especially in such agewes yt
do intermyt come bifits. Among al other old me may best a way with fastig, the
such as be of middell age, after young men, and worse of al children especially
such as be quick and lusty.

Such as grow, have much natural heate within them therefore do require much
meat, which if they have not their bodies do soon consume, but contrary little
meat will ^erue old men, because they have but little natural hete which with
much meat is soon queched, therefore they have not so fervent Agues because
their bodies be cold.

The stomach inward parts be most hot in winter springetime, wherefore men
most then fed better, for ye inward heate the being much doth require much
meat for a proof thereof mark ye ages ye chapios Moist meates be best of al to
such as be sike of agues, chiefly to children, to such as have be acustomed like
meates.

You must mark whether you shall give them meat onse or twyse, and to whom
you must give more, to whom less, and suwhat you most bear with the time of
the year, the cotrey, the age of the person, and with the accustomed use.

In somer and autume men may scarce awai with much meat, but in the winter
best of all, and mean in the spring.

To such as have their sickness bi certain fyttes in order, you shall give
nothing, nether add nor dimynishe before the time of judging.

Here end the Aphorisms of Hyppocrates, set in order for every membre, and
translatyd out of latin into Englyshe by Humfre Lloyd.
A Book conteynyng the names of the compound medecines, which be good for all
ky^de of dyseases that may chance in any membre of mans body, in reading of
which book I would the gentle reader should be admonished of one thing, which is
yt I do comenly through al this book use the latin names, have not translatyd
ye same to ye Englyshe tongue, being moved thereunto, because that many of them
he such that they cannot be well Englished, and also t^at the Apothecaries which
have such medicynes to sell do comenly use the Latyne or rather Arabike, and
Barbarouse terms, and not the Englyshe n^mes thereof, upon which consideracions
I thought it best to use the same through all this present book.
For al diseasys in the head. Capi. i.
THese confections following do not suffer the hears to wax whore gray
electuarium de aromatibus, cofectio alharif, oleu costinum and de alchana.

These be very good for all diseases in the brain, the electuarye of Perles,
Triacle dyatessoron and the confection of musk.

These comfort the brain, aromaticum rofa{rum}: maius aromaticum. dyambra,
galie elephagine pillule stomatice.

These purge the brain, the confectyon alphescera, pillule elephangene,
Oximell squillitike opens ye opilatyon of the brain.

The infusion of hyera heals the melancolike pains of the head.

These be good for the falling evil, confectio de musco, thiriaca diatessaron,
confectio alfescera, syrupus sticados, acetum and oximel squilliticum,
vnguentum de bdellio, oleu de cucumere asmino, de lapide gagatis, de piperibus
and philosophoru. Cofectio alharif kebuli coditi, be very good for al diseasis
in ye senses

These purge ye instruments of ye senses, pillule elephangine stomatiche*
aggregate and pillule lucis maiores and minores.

Hyerapicra purges al cold diseasis of ye head, so doth hiera hermetis,
hieralogodio rufi, pillule aggregate

The cold diseases of the head are healyd with the confectyon of water and
honey.

These confectyons ensuynge are good for all pains in the head, oximell
squillitike, infusyon of Hyeratrociskes of cr^o: oil Anet, oil of Laurel, of
spiknard, of elder oil of wild cucumer,

The infusion of hyera clensith the head, so do pillule stomatice and pillule
aggregate maiores.

Hyera hermetis purges the hemicran, and pillule alhadach an eplayster of
mustard and oil of euforbium heal the same.

The electuary of rosys purgithe the head ache of an hot cause, and so do
pillule alhandach.

These heal the turn or daselynge in the head eyes the confection of musk a
sharpe syroupe of citrones or of prunes, vinegre or oximel squllitike, but
these purge the same hamech, electuarye of Roses, confectio psilii, hyera
hermecis, and hieralogodion ruffi.

For the pains diseases in the ears. Ca. ii.
Oil of bitter almondes, oil of peches and of be, are good for al pains
noise in the ears.

Oil of of Spiknard is good for wynd in the ears.

For al diseases in the eyes. Ca. iii.
THe elec^uarie of Roses purges the superfluites which descend to ye eyes,
also oleum Philosophorum is good for watery eyes.

Pillule de yera, and trifera persica purge al diseasis of the eyes make clear
the sight.

For al diseases in the nose and face. Ca. 4
Oil of wild Cucumer takethe away the steche in the nose and oleum
Philosophorum opens the oppilatyons of the same.

A syrupe of Popy and diacodion with pillule contra catartum, purge heal all
weles which be upon the nose and face.

These cleanse all foul colour, and difformitie of the face, diacucurma,
diamorosion, diacodion, trifera minor, cofectio rauedseni alkakengi, trochiskes
of Roses of rewbarb^.

For al diseasis in the mouth throat. Ca. v.
FOr an Apostem in the throat dyamozo and dyacarido be very good

These confections folowinge be good for them which cannot take their breath,
the confectio of musk loche of squilla, loche of pine, loche ad Asma, Loche
Alfescera, dyasulphur, philoniu, the confection of perles, and alchermes.

Diacodyon and a syrupe of popie heal a room and cough, so do pilbule contra
catarrhum.

Uyneger squillitike heals roten and lose gummes.

Oil of sweet Almondes and of sisami takes away the asperity and roughenesse
of the throat.

Oil of grysomyle takes away all impediments of the tongue.

These confectios make the mouth to have a sweet smell or odour ye electuarie of
atomatikes of perles, of citrones, the confectyo of xiloaloes, aromaticum
muscatum, aromaticu nardinum* trifera saracenica, a syrupe of the pilling of
orenges, mellicrat of orenges, trochiskes of gallia muskata, sufuf xiloaloes,
aromaticum, pillule dyarhodon.

An electuary or syrupe of peches, Peches condite, trochiskes of xiloaloes,
take away all stench in the mouth.

Dyatryonpipereon takes away all belching.

A iulep of iniubes heals al horsnesse.

Diacalamentum, philonium, diacyminu and a syrupe of myntes do utterly stop
al painful and cold yeskyng.

These confectyos of musk, ti^iaca diatesseron sirupus of sticados, the cerote
of alexander, oil of pip^r and oleum philosophoru, hyerahermetis, with
hieralogodio do purge the same wounderful well.

Let him that hath an old painful cough use these, Dianisum, athanasia mag:
if his breast be full of matter, these be good, dyasulphure, loch de pino,
lochsanum with syrupes of myrte, of licori^e* of Calamente, of prunes, of
iniub^s, of Ysope, and these do extenu^te the gross humores loch ad asma susuf
ad Asma, and if they cannot sleep take a syrupe of Popie.

For a cough of a hot cause tak^ loche of popie, loch ad caliditatem a iulep
of violetes, and a syrupe of ye same, with the sirupe contra catarrhu, but if it
be a dry cough, take a syrupe of tereniabine of popie, loch bonum and loch of
almondes.

Pillule de agarico pillule ad omnes morbos catachi, do purge ye matter of an
old cough.

Lochsanum and expertum or a syrupe of iniubes take away horsnes that comes of
cold phlegm.

Oil of Cartamus of nucis indice, of sisami, do clarifi the voice, and so doth
vinegre squillitike.

Musa acnea, oleum philosophoru, be good for the toth ache, and acetu
squilliticum fastens the teeth.

For the morphew yelow iaundes and al other deformyties of the skyne. Capi. vi
THese confectyons make the skyne well colouryd, electuarium de aromatibus,
confectyon of quinces, confectio anacardina, algarif syrup of fumitory, oil of
saffro of cost trifera galeni, the confectio of mana.

Unguentum alfesericu and oleu de cucumere asinino, takes away^ the roughness
of the skin, hamech purges al diseases which be in y^ skin and ye
elephancye.

If you will have your skin smothe clean, use these trifera muskata,
dyacucurma, diamorusio oil of been, of Cherystones, of citrones of elder, of
serpetes, of eggs, of whet of juniper and oil of ash.

Unguentu sericinum is good for to cause the skin to grow.

Unguentu rosaru, violaru, vnguetu ceruse, oleu de iunipero defraxino,
trochiskes of arsenicke do heal wyldfyre and ringwormes.

These confectyos heal the yelow iandes, confectio rauedseni, trifera persica
cofectio de psilio, trochiskes (...) of Rosis, of reubarbe, of camphory and of
enpatori electuariu rosaru, sirupus de fumoterre pillule inde.

Hyeralogodion ruffi, hamech, cofectio epithini, pillule inde, Pillule fetide,
do purge all matter of morphew and leprousy.

Syrupus de fumoterre, and epithimi, oil of iunyper, vnguentum alfesericon. do
heal the leprousy.

Unguentum aragit, oleum de been, de nucleis cerasorum, de granis cittaguloru,
do take away the spott^ of the morphew.

Unguetum alhariel, takes away the spots of the skin.

Pillule Collequintide do purge an old morphewe.

Pillule aggregate minores purge and take away al ytching and skratchynge.

These be good for scabs, oleu nucu, vnguetu cerusae alphesericu.

For al diseases in the stomach. Capi. vii.
AN hard apostem of the stomach is mollified with moist hisop, a cerote of ysop
of galenes descriptyon, dyaquilon with the emplaster of oribasius, and oil of
masticke.

These do styre up appetite ones lost, aromaticum rosatum the confectyon of
quynces, of alchanzi and of orenges, trochiskes of Myrabolanes do increase
appetite wounderfull well.

These confectyons do make good digestyon, dyarodon, acondite of orenges,
aromaticum nardinu, and rosatum, hyeralogodyon ruffi, pillule stomatice,
rosatum maius, diaciminum, diambra, diatrioupipereo kebuli co^diti, a condite
of quinces of buglosse, sufuf xiloalo^s, sufuf aromatu, vinegar squillitike,
trochiskes of rose, pi^lule elephangine, pillule de turbithe.

The confection de galanga, diaciminu oximel squilliticu be good for belchinge

A Table containing ye weightes which phisicyons do comenly use, the
interpretacyon of the names of the compound medicynes herin contained with the
quatitie time yt they ought to be received in.

THe least first of al weightes (comoly used among phisicyons) is a barley corn,
and.xx. corns make a scruple, three scrupules make a drachme, eight drachmes
make an uncle, xii. vnces make apoude. A quarter of poud is three vnces,

And they be this notid.
A corn. gra. A scruple.) A drachme. An uncle.. A pound li. A quarter. q. A
half. s. A handful. m. Ana. of every one.

All compound medycynes be either receyuid within the body, or laid to the
same without* they which be received into ye body be these.

ELectuarium confectio differ in this alone, that electuariu is moist and made
with sugger and honey, confectio dry made alonly with sugar, and because they
be for diverse diseases theris nooe certain time or measure, for the receiving
of them.

Mixtura is when diverse electuaries or cofections be mingled together, is
received.ii. hours be fore meat. Tragea is when diverse pouders be megled
together with sugar and they be received a.. at onest with soppes of strong wine.

Conserua conditu be when diverse spices be mixed with sum sirup and be comely
receiuid early and late after the bygnesse of a walnut.

Loath is a medicine which may be liked with the tongue, may be received at al
times in the quantity of a hasel nut.

Iuleb is a clear potyon made of diverse waters and sugar.

Rob is a joyce made hard thick with the heat of the soon or of ye fire and is
commonly mingled with electuarys, and conserves.

Syrupe is a moist medicine which may be receyuyd early or late

Decoctum is a medicine made of rotes leaves, sead and flowers where unto is
added sugger or honey.

Infusio is when diverse medycins be beaten to powder or hole laid to stepe a
certain space in sum liquor

Trochiscus is a round confectio and plain, made after the manner of a whele,
the which before it be receiuyd most be beaten to powder, and drunk with wine
or other licoure the weight of one. commonly.

Pills be know to al men ought to be received two or three hours at after
supper the quantity of. i.

Sief is a confectyon made after the fashio of a sugar lofe most be dyssoluyd
in liquor before it be receiuid

Collirium is a moist confection made of sief dissolved.

Sufuf is a fine powder made of diverse spices.

Secaniabin is a sharpe syrupe wherein is put sugar or honey.

Masticatoriu is a confection which is held in the mouth chewed to purge the
head of phlegm.

Suffimetum or suffumigatio is when diverse pouders be cast upon the cools,
and the pacyent doth receive the smoke thereof.

Gargarisme is a confectyon of diverse maters and sum decoctyon wherein sum
rob is dissolved, which is gargarised in the mouth and not swalowed down.

Here follow the compound medycynes which be applied to the outward parts of
the body.

UNguetu an ointmet, is made of oils, spices wax, ought hot to be applied to
the place beig somewhat before rubbed with a lynen clothe.

Linimentu is in all points like to vnguetu saving that there goes no wax to
the composityon thereof.

Emplastrum is made of herbs spices, not being beating to powder but a little
bruised mixed with sum liquore or decoctyon, being hot is put upon a line
cloth and so laid so laid to the sore.

Plus dyffereth not from an emplaster saving that meal or bran god to the
composityon thereof.

Cataplasma is made of grene herbs or dry sod in water till they be soft then
applied to the sore.

Cerotu is made of wax or rosyn with oils spices, and is laid upon a cloth cut
after the form of the mebre it should be applied unto.

Dropax is an ointment only used to take away hear.

Sinapismus is an emplaster made of mustard to vlcerate the skin make the
same red.

Epithema is made of diverse pouders mixed with sue ioice or distilled water, and
commonly laid upon scarlet is applied to the seek membre.

Embrocha is when the membre is washed gentilly with a spoge dypt in the
decoction of diverse herbs, rotes and flowers.

Fomentu is a bath made of the decoctyon of diverse herbs to wash the sore
place with al.

Euaporatio is when the diseased membre is holden in ye hot vapour of some
decoctyon.

Saceuly be bags made of linen cloth wherein be coteyned herbs rotes and
leaves which being hot must be first dypte in Wine or vinegar, and then
laid to the membre that is grieved.

Encathisma or insessio is a decoctyon of certain things wherein ye pacyent
most sit for certain space.

The epystle of Diocles unto king Antigonus, which teaches a man to preserve
him self in health.
IN so much that your grace being now somewhat run in years (most noble
Prince Antigonus) is endowed with knowl^dge above other kings, and that in all
parts of Phil^sophy and the arts called Mathematical wherein your grace has
wounderfully profited: I thought that part of Philosophy which teaches a man
to preserve himself in health not worthy to be dyspysed and left untouched of
your regal majesty, wherefore I thought it necessari to declare v^to your
majesty in this Epistle, the causes of diverse diseases with the signs and
tokes which goo before the same, and last of all the remedies wherwyth ^e same
may be healed and cured, for like as the (...) no raging hideous tempest
without sum^ ^anifest and open signs which declare the same to follow, whereby
men which have knowledge and be learned in ye Arcane and privy works of nature
do so provide for themselves that they be sure from all perylles and i^operdyes
that may ensue, so is there no kind of disease or sickness that may infect
any membre of man body but that hath before such evident signs and tokens
that it may be easlye known to follow. Therefore your grace putting your trust
and confidence in those our precepts may easly attain to the perfect and
absolute knowledge of all things.

First of all I have divided the body of man unto four parts, that is to say
the head, the breast, the belly, and the bladder.

Th^se signs and tokens do de^lare when any kind of disease is about to
infect the head, daselyng in the eyes, the headache, heuynesse of y^ brows, a
noise in the ears, prichinge in the temples, the eyes to water in the morning
the sight to fail, with dullness or want of smelling and the lifting up of the
gummes.

When thou doest perceive any such tokens, it is the best remedy to purge
cleanse the head (and that with no purgatyue medicine) but with, v. vnces of
wine made of wytheryd grapes, or of new wine sod till half ^e wasted a way,
therewith thou shalt wash t^y mouth fasting, and gargarise it therein till the
head be purged of phlegm therein contained, and this is the easyest remedy for
al dyseasys in the head. Also it were very good and helthful, if the pacyent
fasting wold eat a quatitie of mustard which have been macerate or steped in
^at^r and honey mingled together, gagarysynge the same wold draw down the
humore contained in the head, but first of all yo^ most take heed the head be
coueryd tyill it h^ar, whereby the slymy phlegm may b^ made more apt mere to
flow down to the mouth.

Now of the contrary part, whose despises these signs and tokens shall be
troubled with these deseases, or one of them, the ophtalmy, ye perle in the
ey^s, brekyng out about the cares poukes or weles in the neck, the c^nsumptyo
in the brain, heuinesse in the head, the squina eye, worms which eat the
hear, the pains in the flape that coueryth the wind pipe, the falling of
the hear, s^abbes or ulcers in the head, and the totheache.

You may perceive by these tokens if any man is like to be diseasyd about the
breast or no, first a sweat through al the body breast the tunge to wax
rough or thyck^, the spittel to be salt or bitter in taste or choleric,
sudden pains in the sides or shulders without manifest occasyon, of tyaning
much watchynge, suffocatyones, thirst after sleep, great sadness, coldness
in the breast, and a shaking in the arms and hands, and the dyseases thereof
ensuing you may avoid with perbraking after a mean supper, without
receyuinge any medicine. Also it is very good to vomyt fasting,

Therefore let him that wold vomit, eat Radyshe, Towneressys, Roket, Mustard*
or purslane, and afterward drink warm wat^r he shall vomyt furthwith, but he
that serrythe lyt^ll by these presagyes and signs ought to fear these
diseasys, the pleurisy, pains in the lunges, melancholical madness, sharpe
agues, the phrenesy, the lythargye, and a burning ague with yeskynge.

When ye belly shall be dyseasyd, sum of these signs do comenly appear
before, the throws and pains in the belly, meates and drinks to ^me bitter,
heuinesse in the knees, cold stiffness in the loins, weariness of al the
body without any occasyon, lack of senses in the legs, and easy fevers,
Now when ^riye of these tokens do appear it is best to make ye belly^ soft and
lose with some kind of dyete and with no purgig medicine, for it is leasse
ieopardye to use such things that a man may scant err in, as betes sod with
water honey, sod garlic, malowes, docks, or mercurye and sweet metes made
with honey, for all these things do mollifye the belly, but if any of the
foresaid signs be manifest or endure lunge add to the said decoctyons the
joyce of b^stard Saffron, for thereby it shall be swetter and more wholesome. Also
Col^wortes sod in a great quantity of water, or four vnces of ye joyce thereof
receyuid with honey and salt, is very good, and of no less effect is the
water of the decoctyon of Cichepcasen or bitterfitch broke fasting, But they
which think these signs to be of none effect, are oftentimes diseased with
these syknesses, the flux in the belly, pains in ye bowels, the lyenceri,
iliaca pa^sio which is a disease in the small guts, the ^ciatica, the fever
tertyan, the gout in ye feet, ye apoplexye the hemorrhoydes, and the joint
syknesse.

Al dyseases of the bladder, ^e know by these tokens, to be very full after
little meat, great in flatyons, much b^lc^ynge, the pale colour of all the
body, heavy or sad sleep, vryne wane of colour, and great pains in the
making there of, with swelling about the pryuye members, after which tokens it
is good to use odoriferouse things which move urine, as the rotes of Fenel or
persely which have ben steped a while in good doriferouse white wine, of yt
which let the pacyent take every morning fasting three vnces with the water af
yelowe carettes or lonage or enula campana, for they be of like operation, of
no less effica^y is ye water wherein Ciches have been steped in, if it be
drunk with wine. But whosoever doth lyghtli passover these tokes shall loke for
sum of these dyseases the hydropsye, the bygnesse of the spleen, pains in the
lyu^r, the stone, pains in the raynes, the strangurye, and th^ d^stentio of
the be^y. And her it is to be noted that in al these signs before rehearsed we
ought to minister gentle and easy medecines to children, and to such as be
elder, medycynes that be of more strong operatyon and greater efficacye.

Now I entende brefly to declare unto your majesty the two turnynges of the
soon callid in latin solstitia (at which times such things do comenli chance)
and what meates your ^ur grace shall use or absteyne from in either of them,
taking my beginning at the winter turnynge.

The winter turn.
Soluitiu ^emale which I call yt witer turn is about ye xi. day of December
when the so enters the Goat.
IN the winter turn do rewmes and humidity increase in means bodies till ye
sprig equinoctial, therefore it is good to eat who^e meates and to drink
sweet wynes and especially with wild marg^ram, and also to use ye company of
women.

There be from the winter turnynge to the spring equinoctial nynty days.

The springtyme equinoctial.
From the spring equinoctial unto the rysynge of the seue sterres called
vergiliac, doth phlegm and sweat corruptyon of the blood engendre in mans
body, The spring equinoctial is ye.x. day of Marche when the son enters the
Rame.
and for that cause it is good to use moist and tart meates, to exercise ye
body, not to absteyne from women, fro the spring equinoctial to the rysynge of
pleyad^s be.xivi. days.

The rysynge of the seven stars.
Choler and vytter matter berythe rule in man from this time unto the somer
turnynge, The seven sters called vergilia^ or p^e^ad{is} rise with the scene about
ye.ix day of may
therefore use meates that be sweet, laxative, beware of acts venereal, fro the
resig^e of p^e^ades unto the somer turn be xlv days.

The somer turnynge.
At this time is melancholy augmentyd tell the heruest equinoctial, therefore
dryncke cold water and smell odoriferouse things, The somer turn is about.x.
of July, when the soon enters the Crab.
as for ^enus you most either use it moderately or exchew it utterly, we have to
the heruest equinoctial nynty and three days.

The heruest equinoctial.
Phlegm thine flurrons abound fro this time to the setting of ye seuyn
sterres, The heruest equinoctial is about ye. 14 of Septebre when the son
enters the balace.
therefore it is good to purge ye humours or to stop ye fluxyons, and to eat
al tart and moist meates, to perbrake nothing at all, to excercyse ye body,
and to flee women, from which time to the setting of the seuin sterres
be.xxxvi. days.

The setting of the seven Sterres.
From this time to the winter turnynge doth phlegm bear domynyon in man, The
seuyn sterres set with the soon about ye.x. of nouebre
therefore you most eat fat bitter things, drink sweet wynes, and excercyse
the body, from the going down of the.vii sterres till the Winter turn be five
and forty days.

Finis.
